Ministry of Industry; Recent News from Wenxi Paper Mill; Increase in Capital to 4.5 Million Yuan; Plant Site Changed to Mawan, West of Wenzhou

Recognizing the weakness of the domestic paper industry and the alarming number of newsprint imports each year, the Ministry of Industry has proposed to establish a factory near Wenzhou, Zhejiang Province, to manufacture newsprint. Since the establishment of the Wenxi Paper Mill Preparatory Committee, it has been actively preparing and sparing no effort. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency learned from the person in charge of the preparatory committee yesterday that the factory's plan is slightly different from what was previously reported in the newspapers. It is said that the factory was originally planned to be located in Wenxi, on the south bank of the Ou River in Yongjia County, Zhejiang Province, using hydroelectric power. That is why the factory was named Wenxi Paper Mill. However, after foreign engineers and experts from the Ministry of Industry went to Wenxi to investigate, they determined that Wenxi's terrain was too low and that there was a risk of flooding in the future. Therefore, after several discussions and several meetings of the preparatory committee and the technical review committee, it was decided that the factory site would not be in Wenxi, but would instead be located in Mawan, 20 kilometers west of Wenzhou, on the north bank of the Ou River. Although the area there is not very large, there is still enough space for future expansion of the factory. The most satisfying thing is that the terrain there is high, and with some filling work, there will be no risk of flooding in the future. As for the future power generation problem, because the stream water flow records are only three years old and are not sufficient to rely on for sufficient water power, and because the construction of a dam would be a huge project that would cost too much, the plan to use hydroelectric power was abandoned. It was decided to use coal-fired steam to power the machinery. In this way, more than one million yuan in costs could be reduced. After the two preconditions of the factory site and the power source were resolved, the paper mill preparatory committee convened its fifth decision-making meeting. The committee members agreed that since the factory site was not located in Wenxi, the original factory name could no longer be used. In order to adapt to the environment and facilitate future foreign trade, it was resolved to change the name to China Paper Corporation and to increase the original capital of 4 million yuan to 4.5 million yuan. Among them, 3.9 million yuan of government shares would be borrowed from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Fund, which is no problem. The public share portion has also been publicly raised. It is reported that after the fifth meeting, the preparatory committee submitted all plans to the Ministry of Industry and requested the Gengzi Fund Board to quickly allocate funds to purchase a large number of machines and purchase land to build the factory buildings.

China Cotton Textile Association Announces Statistics on China's Cotton Industry for the First Half of the Year

Yesterday, the China Cotton Textile Association announced statistics on China's cotton industry for the first half of this year (January to June 1935). The number of spindles in operation was 4,809,559, which is only 12,467 more than the number of spindles in operation in the second half of the previous year (1934), which was 4,797,090. Comparing the two, the number of spindles in operation in the second half of last year increased by 98,820 compared to the first half of last year, and the number of spindles in operation in the first half of last year increased by 80,066 compared to the second half of the previous year. This comparison proves the weakness of the yarn industry. As for the consumption of raw cotton, the total consumption in the first half of this year was 1,172,500 bales (500 pounds per bale), which is also less than the 1,328,000 bales of raw cotton consumed in the second half of last year.

City Chamber of Commerce Submits Another Petition Urging the Enactment of a Law Mandating Compulsory Membership in Trade Associations

Yesterday, the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce submitted a petition to the Ministry of Industry, stating: "Regarding the petition, on the 4th of this month, we received a letter from the Cotton Cloth Trade Association stating that the association's membership, during its peak, reached over 340 firms. Recently, it has dwindled to 163. Comparing members and non-members, the ratio used to be two to three, but now it is one to four. After investigating the reasons, it was found that business declined after the January 28th Incident, with bankruptcies following one after another. This is a secondary cause of the membership decline. However, the main cause is that members must accept various restrictions and fulfill various obligations, while non-members can remain carefree and unrestricted. No one is foolish enough not to emulate the latter's behavior. Although the regulations for the organization of trade associations have been led by your association and followed by various other trade associations, with repeated appeals and strenuous efforts, the legislative authorities only changed the word 'may' to 'should' in the implementing rules regarding membership. Although the meaning is more definite, there is still no compulsory measure against non-members. Therefore, in terms of effectiveness, it is still equal to zero. For example, although various industry regulations stipulate that both members and non-members should comply, compliance is compliance, and disruption is disruption. Since there is no power to force non-members to become members, it is impossible to prevent them from disrupting. In terms of assisting social undertakings, such as national salvation, aviation, water, drought, and other donations, as well as the payment of association and chamber of commerce fees, everything must be taken from the members, while non-members do not contribute. They are engaged in the same business, so why favor them over us? How can the group achieve soundness and prevent the members from scattering? Our association, considering the current situation, feels that unless membership in the association is compulsory for all those in the same industry, the function of the group cannot be brought into play, and the foundation of the association cannot be consolidated. Therefore, at the sixth members' general meeting held on August 31st, upon the proposal of fellow members, it was decided to write to the City Chamber of Commerce to forward to the government authorities, requesting the swift formulation of compulsory measures for non-members, etc. Considering the above reasons, we respectfully submit this letter, hoping you will investigate and handle it, and we look forward to a reply.

Upon receiving this letter, the issue of formulating methods for implementing compulsory membership has been a long-standing and unresolved problem for years. The subordinate associations have repeatedly presented the critical situation of various industries. On April 15th, we submitted a request to your association to incorporate the instructions in the approval No. 29205 of October of the previous year into the implementing rules so that they could be used as a basis for court prosecution when necessary. Subsequently, at the sixth members' general meeting of the subordinate association on June 23rd, members again proposed a motion to formulate compulsory membership measures. It was again resolved to submit a petition to your ministry on June 24th based on the original petition of April 15th, urging a swift handling of the matter. To date, no approval has been received. In recent years, local and central authorities have entrusted the trade associations with commercial surveys and national salvation, water, drought, aviation, and other donations. However, in reality, the scope of membership is limited, and the power to call upon is extremely weak. The cotton cloth industry, which is a relatively well-established and long-standing organization, is still as described in the original letter, and the rest need not be discussed. The strength of the organization of various industries depends on the outcome of this case. We have been eagerly awaiting for several years. It is reasonable to truthfully submit this report, hoping that your ministry will review and approve the various sections submitted previously and promptly discuss and implement them, which would be in the public interest."

Stamp Duty on Bills of Lading Issued by Shipping Companies: Still Handled According to the Old Rules

The Shipping Industry Association sent a letter to its members, stating: "Regarding the implementation of the Stamp Duty Law on September 1st, our association believes that the tax rate stipulated in Article 16, Tariff Table, Item 12, of the law, which requires a stamp duty of 20 cents per bill of lading, is too heavy and cannot be borne. On August 17th, we sent a telegram to the Legislative Yuan requesting a revision to reduce the tax rate. The freight income from bills of lading for goods transported along the coast is sometimes less than one national currency unit, while the income of forwarding companies or freight forwarders from bills of lading is often higher than that of shipping companies. However, Item 13 of the same article stipulates that forwarding companies or freight forwarders' bills of lading only require a stamp duty of 2 cents. This comparison is unfair. Moreover, Item 12 of the same article stipulates that bills of lading issued by public shipping enterprises are exempt from stamp duty, which is inconsistent with the principle stated in the Provisional Constitution that the government should encourage and protect private shipping. Furthermore, the Japanese shipping companies' bills of lading only require a stamp duty of 3 cents per bill. Therefore, we have specifically requested the revision of the article based on the aforementioned reasons and facts.

After the Legislative Yuan sent out the telegram, our association also sent separate petitions to the Ministry of Finance, requesting them to forward the petition and to instruct their subordinates to allow the old rules to be followed until the Legislative Yuan approves the revision. At the same time, we also sent a letter to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to review and forward the petition as soon as possible, requesting that the tax be reduced to ensure fairness and to maintain the shipping industry. Now, we have received a letter from the Secretariat of the Legislative Yuan, stating that the President of the Yuan has issued an incoming telegram, which states that Article 16, Item 12, of the Stamp Duty Law stipulates that a stamp duty of 20 cents per shipping bill of lading is too heavy and requests a revision to reduce the tax, etc. The approval was given to the Finance Committee for review. In addition to forwarding this to you for your review, etc., the association's request to revise the article and reduce the stamp duty on shipping bills of lading has been accepted by the Legislative Yuan, and there is hope that the revision will be approved. The association, fearing that the stamp duty enforcement agency might be too lenient in its punishments, has recently submitted a further petition to the Ministry of Finance, stating that the case has been accepted by the Legislative Yuan and requesting that its subordinates be instructed to review the case and continue to handle the stamp duty on shipping bills of lading according to the old rules. This is the process by which the association petitioned to revise the article, reduce the stamp duty on shipping bills of lading, and request that its subordinates be instructed to handle the case according to the old rules.

According to the investigation, Shanghai shipping bills of lading have traditionally been divided into those issued at the South Customs and those issued at the North Customs. Those issued at the South Customs are for goods from the inland. The association invited its members to discuss this matter in 1928. The members agreed that since the bills of lading do not specify the amount of money, it would be difficult to affix stamps according to the progressive method. They requested that a uniform stamp duty of 4 cents be affixed to each bill. Subsequently, the Shanghai South District Branch of the Jiangsu Stamp Duty Office replied that it was not convenient to change the tax rate without authorization. The matter was presented to the Director-General of the General Office when he was in Jin Province, and he was asked for instructions on how to handle the matter. He also stated that it was not convenient to freely change the legally prescribed regulations. Even if there were obstacles and difficulties in implementation, it was necessary to request the government to revise the regulations through legal procedures. Currently, the average stamp duty affixed to each bill of lading is 4 cents, which is too different from the originally determined tax rate, and it is difficult to approve in practice. Now, it has been found that some provincial shipping bills of lading affix a stamp duty of 10 cents per bill. Although this is still inconsistent with the progressive method stipulated in the regulations, it does not damage tax revenue. For the convenience of merchants, it seems that a temporary expedient method can be adopted, etc. This was sent to you for review and to inform the various shipping companies that all bills of lading must affix a stamp duty of 10 cents per bill to ensure uniformity and avoid disputes, etc. This is the situation regarding stamp duty on bills of lading issued at the South Customs. As for the North Customs, the goods are those from trading ports. The association invited the customs declaration offices to discuss this matter. Subsequently, a reply was received stating that the General Chamber of Commerce had previously sent a letter regarding the affixing of stamp duty to bills of lading. The representative of the Ministry of Finance stated that the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs had submitted a report stating that the tax and levy bills mentioned in the Chamber of Commerce's letter were tantamount to taxing taxes. According to Category 2 of the Stamp Duty Regulations, stamps were originally affixed to bills of lading. However, in order to facilitate merchants, an expedient method was adopted to change the practice to affixing stamps to tax and levy bills according to the amount, which is not a tax on taxes, etc. This was forwarded to you for review and then notified to the various industries for compliance. Therefore, the stamp duty on bills of lading has already been ordered to be affixed to tax and levy bills. Therefore, Tian Yong will not participate in the matter again, etc. This is the situation regarding stamp duty on bills of lading issued at the North Customs. Because the methods in the North and South cities are different, the association can only request that the old rules continue to be followed. Fearing that the various chambers of commerce may not be clear about this, we have included this information for your reference. We hereby issue this notice, hoping that you will review and handle it."

The Shanghai Shipping Industry Association announced yesterday that some shipping companies charge as little as 50 cents of national currency for freight income from bills of lading. Some ships issue hundreds of bills of lading per voyage. However, Article 16, Item 12 of the Stamp Duty Law, which came into effect on September 1st, stipulates that a stamp duty of 20 cents must be affixed to each shipping bill of lading, which is too heavy a tax rate and unfair, and cannot be borne by shipping merchants. Moreover, the same article states that bills of lading issued by public shipping enterprises are exempt from stamp duty, which is inconsistent with the principle of Article 36 of the Provisional Constitution that the state should encourage and protect private shipping. The association has petitioned the government to revise the article to reduce the tax and requested equal treatment with public enterprises. At the same time, it has requested the authorities to temporarily handle the matter according to the old rules before the revision is made. We hereby issue this notice for your public consideration.

Children's Year of Happiness: Matters Requiring Attention by Charitable Organizations

The Match Industry Federation Sends a Letter to the City Chamber of Commerce, Detailing Its Opinions on the New Stamp Duty Law, Considering That There Are Discrepancies with Legal Intent and Omissions, Requesting Further Discussion and Submission to the Ministry of Finance for Revision and Supplementation

The new Stamp Duty Law and its Implementing Rules have been promulgated by the National Government and came into effect on September 1st. The China National Match Industry Federation of this city believes that there are still two points in the provisions of the law that are worth discussing, and has specially sent a letter to the City Chamber of Commerce, requesting further research and submission to the Ministry of Finance for revision. The original text is recorded below:

Officially Promulgated

Respectfully stated, the "Stamp Duty Law" and its "Implementing Rules" have been implemented by the government since September 1st. We would like to present our views on the points that can be discussed, as far as we can see. Article 3 of the Stamp Duty Law lists various documents that are exempt from stamp duty, and Item 8 stipulates, "All documents used internally by public or private organs or organizations that do not generate external rights and obligations." This means that these documents can be exempted from stamp duty as long as they are used internally by the organ or organization and do not generate external relations. The organ or organization is clearly regarded as a whole system, without any distinction between the head office and branch offices, and without any distinction between mutual use between the head office and branch offices. Whether interpreted from the text or spirit of the law, there is no doubt about this. However, the latter part of Article 4 of the Implementing Rules states that "mutual use between the second-level organ and the head office, or between the branch organization and the head organization, shall not be regarded as internal use," which actually distorts the entire system that is clearly recognized by the law, forcibly divides it, and says that "documents used internally and not generating external rights and obligations" shall not be regarded as internal use." Not only does this

Clearly Violate Legal Intent

It is also close to arbitrariness. This association is a match industry group. Although it is impossible to know the contents of other public or private organs or organizations in detail, as far as match companies are concerned, they generally set up a head office in a place with convenient transportation for centralized management, and set up branch offices and factories in other suitable locations to undertake the responsibilities of sub-management and manufacturing. All work allocation and operating profits and losses are handled by the head office, which bears full responsibility. This is because the company is a legal person, its personality is conferred by law, and its rights and obligations are similar to those of natural persons. Therefore, the separate establishment of its head office, branch offices, and factories is like the separate forms of the head and limbs of a natural person. Although there are distinctions on the surface, they are actually an integral whole and cannot be separated for a moment, let alone forcibly split. Therefore, the documents mutually notified between the head office, branch offices, and factories are completely an entire act and cannot be divided into a branch organ and a head office, or a branch organization and a head organization. The stamps affixed to the documents and securities issued by them are the same as the legal principle of Article 8 of the same article. The Implementing Rules regard the provisions that legal persons should have in Article 4 of the first item of this law as something that has not been

Explained in Any Way

For Article 8, it even forcibly interprets it as a branch organ and a head organ, or a branch organization and a head organization, saying that "the documents used internally and not generating external rights and obligations shall not be regarded as internal use." In terms of legal principles, it is self-contradictory. This Implementing Rule should be carefully revised. Article 16, Item 4 of the Stamp Duty Law stipulates that the work ledger used by workers in various industries to withdraw wages is exempt from stamp duty, and Article 27 of the same article stipulates that the employment guarantee is also exempt from stamp duty. Because workers have a difficult life, their work ledgers and guarantees, which they rely on to withdraw wages, are specially exempted from tax to show consideration. The law is well-intentioned and deeply admirable. However, whether a worker's employment contract should be

Exempt from Stamp Duty

Although the law does not have explicit provisions, it seems that it should also be included in the exemption list according to the above exemption rules. The Implementing Rules should deeply embody the legal intent and add explanations and supplements. However, after reading the provisions of the Implementing Rules, I did not pay attention to this, which seems to be a failure to thoroughly implement the legal intent of caring for workers, which is regrettable. This Implementing Rule should be carefully supplemented. I think that the law should be observed, and research should be pursued in detail. The two points mentioned above seem to have room for research. Your association is a leader in the business community, and you have a proven record of research on the Stamp Duty Law. I dare not refuse to express my humble opinions and have explained them in detail in separate letters. I hope you will discuss them and, if you agree, forward them to the Ministry of Finance and make appropriate revisions and supplements to the above-mentioned discrepancies and omissions in the Implementing Rules that are inconsistent with the legal intent. I am most grateful to the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce and the China National Match Industry Federation."

The Theft of Rickshaws in Nanshi Flaring Up Again

Since the Nanshi rickshaw theft and ransom cases were addressed by the Rickshaw Pullers Trade Association organizing a "No Ransom Group," and the Municipal Public Security Bureau earnestly investigated and apprehended notorious offenders like Xiao Su San, Han Tuozi, and Xiao Heizi, handing them over to the local court, and the French Concession Police also captured Wang Degui, Xu San Xiazi, and Xiao Fuzi, rickshaw theft cases in the Nanshi area had gradually decreased and almost disappeared. Previously, when a rickshaw puller had his cart stolen, he had to seek help from various sources and be familiar with the procedures, costing him at least fifteen or sixteen yuan to get compensated. If the rickshaw was lost without a trace, the loss was unimaginable. Thanks to the Association's relief efforts, the compensation for a stolen rickshaw was only six yuan, and if the cart was recovered, three yuan would be refunded. Therefore, the rickshaw pullers were deeply grateful. However, recently, the ringleaders of these rickshaw thefts, who have been living off this unexpected income for many years, are unwilling to change to other professions. Besides sending their accomplices to steal rickshaws in the Zhabei, Hongqiao, and Anglo-French Concessions to hold them for ransom, they are also taking advantage of the night to operate in various rickshaw depots in Nanshi. When no one is there to negotiate a ransom, they strip the carts of their tires and leave them on the road. The rickshaw depots have appealed to the Association for relief. The Association, considering that the "No Ransom Group" was established for rickshaw pullers whose carts were stolen outside, only agreed to submit a request to the authorities for investigation and also issued leaflets urging each rickshaw depot to be careful to avoid inadvertently encouraging theft. Therefore, each rickshaw depot is mutually vigilant at night. Ringleaders such as Lu A Si, Zhao Xiao Sizi, and Liu Cheng Song are very active, hoping to undermine the "No Ransom Group" organization. It is deeply hoped that the municipal authorities will pay close attention.

Western Servant Demands Wages, Accused of Murder by Employer, Witness Proves Defendant Not Seen with Knife, Bail Approved for Defendant on the 11th

Huang Ji Hai, from Wuhu, was a Western servant at the home of a German doctor, Dr. Fox (transliterated), at 810 Route Petain in the French Concession. After being dismissed on the 22nd of last month, he went to the employer at about 7 PM that afternoon to settle his wages, which he did not receive. He was then injured in the head by a meat cleaver thrown at him, causing bleeding. He was also knocked to the ground and beaten, and his right arm was scalded with boiling water. He escaped and reported to the police station and was sent to the hospital for treatment. Instead, Fox reported to the police station that Huang had attempted to kill him with a knife and requested an investigation. Thereupon, the police station transferred Huang to the Second Special Court, filed a public prosecution, and detained him. Details have already been published in this newspaper. Yesterday, Judge Wang Xu Chang of the Second Special Court revisited the case in the Criminal Division. According to Huang's statement, he first demanded wages that day and was pushed out the door. When he went in a second time, he was injured in the head, causing bleeding. After being knocked to the ground and brutally beaten, his arm was scalded with boiling water. With both hands held, how could he have held a knife to kill his employer? He didn't know where the knife came from and requested a thorough investigation. The rest of his statement was the same as previously reported. His monthly salary was twenty yuan, and he was due for payment on the 22nd. He requested a settlement, etc. According to the translated statement of the plaintiff, Fox, "He (referring to Huang) came to demand wages, so I ordered someone to go out to exchange foreign dollars because he looked very fierce when he came. Therefore, I pushed him out the door. The second time he came in, I saw he was about to hit me, so I held both his hands. I saw a knife behind him fall to the ground. I never hit him," etc. At this point, the court considered the facts to be clear and ordered the commencement of arguments. First, Attorney Fei Xizhen of the Police Department argued, stating that the Police Department based its prosecution on the plaintiff's accusation and prosecuted for attempted murder. However, the witnesses testified that they did not see the defendant with a knife, nor did they prove that the defendant had any murderous behavior. The charge of attempted murder cannot be sustained. He requested that the court judge the case according to law. The defendant, represented by Attorney Gu Jirong, defended based on the facts, the law, and the testimonies of the witnesses and the defendant. The court adjourned the proceedings and scheduled the verdict for the 11th. The defendant was ordered to post a bail of one thousand yuan and a shop guarantee to appear whenever summoned. After repeated requests from the defendant's attorney to reduce the amount, the judge granted permission. The defendant changed to posting a bail of four hundred yuan with a shop guarantee to await further instructions.

National Diocesan Congress of the Chinese Catholic Action Society Held, Approximately 200 Representatives Attending for One Week Starting Tomorrow

The first National Diocesan Congress of the Chinese Catholic Action Society is scheduled to open tomorrow morning (the 8th) in the hall of Gongjin Middle School, located near the St. Joseph's Hospital on Guohuo Road in Nanshi. The Society is organized by Chinese Catholics. This conference is of great importance and significance to the nation and religion. A reporter from the Central News Agency specifically visited Bishop Yu Bin, the supervisor of the current Congress, at the Dongjiadu Catholic Church in Nanshi and learned the following about the Society's past and the current Congress:

Organization Process

The Chinese Catholic Action Society was initiated by Catholics in the North 25 years ago. Twenty-three years ago, Lu Bohong, the current General Manager of the Shanghai Chinese Merchants Electric Company, started organizing and promoting it. It is a group of purely Chinese Catholics outside the Catholic clergy and laity mixed organizations. The members of the Society, feeling the peril of the nation and the suffering of the people, love their motherland, which is also one of the tenets of Catholicism. They want to use the collective strength of the 3 million Catholics in China to affirm their will. On the one hand, they want to reform the past attitude of self-cultivation in isolation; on the other hand, they want to lay the foundation for the future, so as to benefit the nation and the people and promote Christian doctrines. That is why this Society was convened. The topics for discussion are nothing more than charity, society, education, and evangelization.

Attending Representatives

Preparations for this Congress have been underway for a year and can now be held. Except for the special circumstances in the Northeast, which made it impossible to participate, there are 211 dioceses across the country, as well as representatives from places like Southeast Asia, with over 200 representatives attending. As of last night, one-third of the representatives had arrived in Shanghai, and the rest of the representatives are expected to arrive before 8 PM tonight. Because from 8 PM tonight until tomorrow morning, the attending representatives will all participate in the Catholic retreat. The representatives are staying at Zhengxiu Middle School. The Congress is scheduled for one week, from September 8th to September 15th. On September 16th, they are free to participate in the pilgrimage to Our Lady of Sheshan.

Congress Staff

The honorary chairman of this Congress is Ma Xiangbo, the chairman is Lu Bohong, the general supervisor is Gan Bin, and Archbishop Cai, the representative of the Pope, will attend. The Pope also has a handwritten letter praising the Society, which has been translated into various languages and will be read publicly at the opening ceremony.

Today's and Tomorrow's Schedule

Dinner is at 7 PM tonight, and at 8 PM, participants will enter the church to listen to the retreat sermon. Tomorrow morning, participants will wake up at 5 AM (every day thereafter). At 5:30 AM, they will enter the church to listen to the retreat sermon, attend Mass, and receive Communion. Breakfast is at 7 AM. At 8 AM, they will participate in Archbishop Cai's High Mass at Puyutang, specifically praying to St. Joseph. At 10 AM, the opening ceremony of the Congress will be held (at the auditorium of Zhengxiu Middle School). The order is as follows: (1) Music entry, (2) Ringing the bell to open the meeting, (3) Recitation of the invocation of the Holy Spirit, (4) Salute to the Catholic flag, (5) Singing the Congress song, (6) The Pope's representative reads the Pope's handwritten letter and delivers the opening speech, (7) Bishop Hui delivers a speech, (8) President of the General Association delivers a speech, (9) Guest speakers deliver speeches, (10) General Supervisor reports, (11) Reciting the Lord's Prayer to close the meeting, (12) Music, (13) Photography. At 3 PM in the afternoon, the proposals review committee will meet and the groups will start working. At 5 PM, there will be a lecture (at the auditorium of Zhengxiu Middle School). The order is as follows: (1) Ringing the bell to open the meeting, (2) Reciting the scripture, (3) Chairman's report, (4) Bishop Hui lectures on "What the Holy Church Expects from Catholic Action Society Members," (5) Bishop Cheng lectures on the history of the evolution of Chinese Catholic Action Society, (6) Reciting the scripture to close the meeting. At 7 PM, there will be a blessing of the Blessed Sacrament, and at 7:30 PM, there will be a large banquet.

Congress Schedule

Two Right Feet Found at the Entrance of Ciyunfang, Wangzhi Road, Examination Reveals They Are Amputated and Preserved Specimens, Police Order Investigation to Find the Person Who Abandoned Them

At 0:20 PM the day before yesterday, two abandoned human feet, one fetus, and one piece of muscle were discovered at the side of a urinal near a trash can at the entrance of Ciyunfang Lane, No. 222 Wangzhi Road in the French Concession. The discovery caused a commotion, and many people gathered to watch. A patrolman reported the discovery to the Xiafei Road police station, which dispatched detectives to investigate. At the same time, the feet, fetus, etc., were transported to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for examination. Details have already been published in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that one of the feet seemed to have been amputated due to bullet wounds sustained in battle, while the other seemed to have been amputated due to illness. The fetus appeared to be from a five- or six-month-old miscarriage, and the piece of muscle was a leg muscle that had been cut off due to illness and was not from the buttocks or anus. Yesterday morning, the police station reported to the Second Special Court Procuratorate, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren to visit the scene with coroner Jiang and clerk Peng at noon. After a clear examination, it was determined that they were specimens that had been cut off, made into specimens, and then abandoned. After the examination was completed, the case was filed. According to the investigating detective Zhang Chunsheng's report on the investigation, the official instructed that it was determined that the two human right feet (one of which was amputated due to injury) were all specimens that had been sawed off and preserved. The fetus (approximately five or six months old) and a piece of thigh meat were also abandoned specimens and were handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Hall for burial. The case of the abandonment of the corpse will be handled by the police. After the examination, the Tongren Fuyuan Branch instructed the workers to put the two feet and thigh meat together in a small coffin and the fetus in another small coffin and carry them to the cemetery for burial. It is also said that about half an hour before the discovery, a seven- or eight-year-old child saw a man holding a paper package, going to the entrance of Ciyunfang Lane, and throwing it into the trash can. At that time, the child wanted to pick it up and open it, but the man immediately stopped him and said that there was a dead child inside and it was not to be opened and looked at. Then, he gave the child a few copper coins and waved him away. Later, the child did not walk far and saw the man go away. He invited a few children to pick up the paper package, opened it, and saw that it was a human foot and a dead child. He was greatly shocked and threw it on the ground and fled, causing passersby to gather and spread the news far and wide. The police station is now fully dispatching detectives to investigate and arrest the person who abandoned them for interrogation.

Municipal Council Discusses Rickshaw Puller Issues

The Municipal Council held its first meeting after the autumn break the other day. The most important topic discussed that day was the issue of rickshaw pullers. The content of this issue is very complex and of great concern to the general public. On that day, Chairman Massey of the Vehicle Committee first presented a report. According to the report, as of July 31, the number of rickshaw pullers who had already obtained licenses was 37,135. The total number of registered rickshaw pullers in mid-August was 41,909. It is also planned to continue to handle the registration and licensing, and it is expected that the number of licensed rickshaw pullers will reach 42,000 by the end of October. Those who fail the inspection will also reach 1,100 or 1,200. (The previous report of 12,000 was a typo.) In this way, those who are already engaged in pulling rickshaws can have the opportunity to obtain a license to make a living. It is heard that the Municipal Council has expressed its approval of this proposal.

Lake Society Paints Alerting Pictures, Distributes to Six Counties for Posting to Avoid Women Being Deceived

The six counties of the Lake District are areas of wealth in western Zhejiang. The soil is fertile and the products are abundant. Silk is a major product. Rural life has always been stable. However, in recent years, there have been successive droughts and floods, and there has been no peaceful year. The price of silk has also fallen drastically, leading to rural bankruptcy and economic hardship. Some intellectually weak rural women are not content with staying at home, and cunning vagrants take this opportunity to visit and, using the excuse of finding work, deceive them to come to the city, plotting to sell them and cause them to fall into other places. Previously, the Lake Society of this city printed and distributed vernacular exhortations to the counties and this trend subsided somewhat. Recently, it was heard that old habits have been revived. For the sake of a fundamental solution, the Society specially asked famous artists to paint various warning pictures of the various tragic situations suffered by deceived women, printed them in three-color plates, and distributed them to the townships and towns of the six counties for posting, in order to educate the public and prevent rural women from being deceived and going astray.

Peach Garden Lane: The Internal Workings of the "Red Pill" Scheme; The Profound Involvement of a Woman Named Pang; Willing to Pay a Thousand Taels to Bribe Police

Upstairs in a carpenter's shop at No. 163 Peach Garden Lane, North Jiangxi Road, someone was secretly manufacturing a machinery for making drug pills. Around 5:00 AM on the 29th of last month, a man from Taizhou named Luo Zhaoxiu suddenly jumped from the building, attempting to escape. He injured his buttocks and was unable to stand. Tang Fuxiang, a carpenter's apprentice, saw him and reported it to Detective No. 1894, who arrived and took him to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the injuries were minor, and he recovered within a few hours. Subsequently, he and the landlord, Zhu Mao, went upstairs and confiscated a large leather suitcase containing the raw materials for making the drug pills: morphine, caffeine, saccharin, resin, white powder, etc., totaling 26 different ingredients. They also apprehended two people: Madam Pang Li from Hangzhou and Yang Renchu from Guangdong. Together with a large quantity of the manufactured "red pills," they were taken to the Hongkou Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi opened the Third Criminal Court for examination. The Municipal Council solicitor, Li Zhishan, stated that during the adjournment, the defendant, Madam Pang Li, claimed she was looking for a job at a job broker in a small vegetable market on Avenue Road, but had not found one, and was just lingering on the floor above the workshop. Her statement was unreliable. When arrested, she offered Detective No. 1894 one thousand yuan to be released, but was refused. Furthermore, the landlord, Zhu Mao, had been sending people to collect rent for the past two months, and Madam Pang had been paying it, but did not allow anyone to enter the room. At the time, the reason Luo Zhaoxiu jumped from the building was that he had been instructed by the main suspect, surnamed Zhang, to Yang Renchu to be careful, as competitors in the French Concession had discovered the location of the workshop. They were jealous and wanted to create trouble. At that time, many people came to the building to investigate, and Yang Renchu escaped via the roof and fled through a neighboring house. Luo Zhaoxiu, in desperation, jumped from the window and was injured. Madam Pang was out at the time. This was the summary of the investigation. When questioned, Madam Pang Li, looking ill, claimed to be suffering from typhoid fever and had nothing to do with the manufacturing of the red pills. Her testimony was extremely evasive. Solicitor Li said that she was heavily addicted to opium and "yue" pills, making her appearance gaunt. Since being detained, she had been unable to indulge. The typhoid fever was likely a fabrication. The defendant, Yang Renchu, testified that the owners of the workshop were two people surnamed Zhang who were on the run, and only came two or three times a week. He claimed to be just a worker. Luo Zhaoxiu testified that he was introduced to the place by his brother, initially as a cook, and then replaced Yang Renchu and the two Zhangs in helping to manufacture the "red pills." Judge Jiang ordered the defendants to be remanded in custody separately and scheduled sentencing.

Zhejiang Industrial Bank: Embezzlement by Employee Concluded; Sentencing Scheduled for the 13th

The case of embezzlement by Wang Liangjie, an employee of Zhejiang Industrial Bank, was heard again yesterday morning. Presiding Judge Feng Shide of the First Special District Court took his seat in the First Court. The police lawyer presented the results of the investigation during the adjournment and stated that the previous claim of an additional deposit of 2,800 yuan in the Chunji account involving collusion with the chief officers was incorrect. Judge Feng questioned the defendant about the embezzlement. The defendant's testimony was evasive, only stating that the embezzlement was true because of high family expenses and many requests for loans from relatives and friends. He therefore resorted to this tactic and requested leniency. Subsequently, the agent of Zhejiang Industrial Bank requested an incidental civil suit, ordering the defendant to repay 41,155.17 yuan. However, they stated that after the defendant was handed over to the police, the defendant's friend returned a loan of over 10,000 yuan, part of which had been deposited with the police. The actual amount the plaintiff sought to recover in the incidental civil suit should be 31,282.07 yuan. Judge Feng instructed the defendant's defense lawyer to provide a lawful defense. He then ordered sentencing on the 13th of this month and adjourned the court.

Ruan Kaiji Case Concluded; Sentencing Scheduled for the 11th of This Month

The case in which Madam Tu Xu sued Mei Weiyu, who ran the Jiang Xiangxing slaughterhouse, and Ruan Kaiji, head of the Xin Zha sub-bureau, for restricting her freedom, etc., has been heard repeatedly by the Criminal Court of the District Court without resolution. Details have been previously reported. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Tan Zhuohong specially opened the Eleventh Court for continued hearing. The plaintiff, along with lawyer Lu Qi, appeared in court and presented the previous facts. The defendant, Jiang Weiyu, hired lawyers Zhang Fukang and Huang Qiying to defend him. According to Ruan Kaiji's testimony, the Tu Xu case was investigated by police officer Ouyang. Tu Xu should have been released, but the plaintiff, Jiang Weiyu, requested that her husband, Tu Axiang, be related to the strike case. As for the handcuffs, it was the general practice of the headquarters, and all defendants had to be handcuffed. According to Jiang Weiyu's testimony, Tu Axiang and Tu Xu voluntarily went to the bureau to explain the matter. Ouyang Liu testified that on that day, Tu Xu was questioned and ordered to sign a bond for release. Because the plaintiff requested that she be sent to headquarters, she was transferred to headquarters the next day for handling. At this point, lawyer Lu Qi stated that the main culprit was Ouyang alone, and Ruan Kaiji was suffering for someone else's fault. Ouyang replied, "I ordered her to leave." Tu Xu said to Ouyang, "What business is it of yours to confine me for a night? If you told me to leave, I wouldn't leave. There's no such idiot in the world." The judge questioned the two police officers and then ordered the start of the debate. Lawyers Zhang and Huang gave lengthy and eloquent arguments. The judge stated that the case was clear and concluded the debate, scheduling sentencing for the 12th.

Xie Jingjiang Attempts to Murder His Wife; Wife Sues for Divorce; Forced into Prostitution by an Anmo Girl; Ye Xiangru's Plight is Also Pitiful

In the Lidu Anmo Parlor at the intersection of Sichuan Road and Old Barracks Road, there is an anmo girl named Ye Xiangru (also known as Aidi) from Nanjing, who is 21 years old. In 1929, when Xiangru was 15 years old, she was married to Xie Jingjiang from Ningbo through a matchmaker named Zhang. The couple's relationship was harmonious. Xie worked as a servant for a foreigner, but was dismissed for poor performance. After losing his job, he had difficulty maintaining his livelihood and repeatedly borrowed money from his wife, which was refused. Last month, Xie rushed to the anmo parlor and tricked his wife out the door. He pulled out a sharp knife and tried to kill Xiangru. The owner of the parlor, Mr. Chen, saw it and immediately stepped forward to dissuade him. Xiangru reported it to the Central Police Station. After questioning, the head detective determined that it was a common dispute between husband and wife and refused to handle it. At this point, Xiangru had no choice but to hire a lawyer and file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court for divorce. Yesterday morning, Judge Mo Runhua specially opened the civil court for hearing. The plaintiff, Ye Xiangru, along with her attorney, appeared in court. The defendant was absent. The plaintiff testified that she married the defendant at the age of fifteen and held a formal wedding at the Zuile Village Restaurant on Wusong Road, renting a house at No. 315 Xin Xin Li, Dapei Bridge, Rue du Pere Robert in the French Concession. It has been seven years since then, and they have one child. Working in an anmo parlor is a last resort, forced by the defendant. She also stated that she had received a considerable education and disregarded her honor due to the pressure of making a living. Judge Mo adjourned the case due to the defendant's absence and scheduled a hearing for testimony.

Lu Wenzhong Sues Women's Bank; Erroneous Legal Citations; Amended Complaint; Rescheduled Hearing

Because of past deposit transactions between the Women's Bank and the United Trading Company's Lu Wenzhong, a checkbook was provided to Lu, so that Lu could use the checks to access funds. Recently, however, the bank has been returning Lu's signed checks. The reason for refusing payment was merely to write "Please contact the drawer" on the returned checks. However, Lu audited his accounts with the bank and found that he still had a balance, which should not be refused. This caused damage to his external reputation. He sent a letter to the bank asking for an explanation and requesting a statement. Later, he learned that the bank claimed that although there were still funds in his current account, there were arrears in other accounts, and that after offsetting the two, there was still a shortage. Therefore, the checks were stopped. However, Lu believed that the bank's action of "planting flowers and grafting trees" was inappropriate. He hired a lawyer Liu Lun to file a criminal complaint against the chairman of the bank, Yao Muhua, and others, requesting that they be punished for breach of trust. The First Special District Court accepted the complaint, noting that the legal provisions cited by the plaintiff were not entirely appropriate for the matter. Therefore, in the afternoon, Judge Pan Fen held a hearing and summoned the plaintiff to court, informing him that the bank's refusal to honor the checks was a civil dispute and did not constitute a crime of breach of trust. He explained the elements of a crime of breach of trust in detail. Finally, he told him that if he wanted to sue, the legal provisions would have to be amended. The plaintiff's lawyer, upon hearing this, said that he would discuss the amendment of the legal provisions with his client and then amend the complaint. The court then granted an adjournment for further investigation.

United Rent Reduction Association of Various Districts: Notice to Branch Associations in Various Districts; Beware of People Using the Name to Collect Fees Under False Pretenses

The Shanghai United Rent Reduction Association of Various Districts, because the city-wide association has virtually ceased, only the First Special District Association has taken its place. However, the work outside the Special District is not widespread enough. Furthermore, with the market declining daily, rent reduction is becoming increasingly urgent. Therefore, the rent reduction associations of various districts in the city have formed the Shanghai United Rent Reduction Association of Various Districts, actively planning, cooperating, and dividing labor, with the goal of achieving universal rent reduction as soon as possible. It has recently been heard that there are unscrupulous people using the name of the General Rent Reduction Association, deceiving and confusing people, and collecting fees everywhere, undermining the people's movement. Inevitably, there may be other intentions. The United Association has issued an urgent notice to branch associations in various districts to pay attention, and sent letters to police stations and concessions to strictly investigate. The original letter is as follows: "To Whom It May Concern: The Rent Reduction Association was originally organized out of necessity due to social environmental conditions, in order to alleviate the livelihood of ordinary people. This kind of people's movement is extremely important. However, all the expenses of the association are borne by the district associations, and no fees are collected from the outside. This has already been published in the newspaper. It has recently been heard that hundreds of people are using the name of the general association to deceive and confuse people, collecting fees everywhere under false pretenses, which is tantamount to fraud and is greatly inconsistent with the original purpose of rent reduction. It is obviously intended to undermine the legitimate people's movement, so it is impossible to remain silent. In addition to sending letters to branch associations in various districts to notify all tenants, if they encounter the above situation, they should immediately investigate. We are writing to you to request that you send personnel to investigate as soon as possible to prevent illegal activities. Sincerely, etc."

Miss Xiong Zhi Departs Today to Visit Charitable Institutions in Europe and America

Miss Xiong Zhi, the eldest daughter of former Prime Minister Xiong Xiling, a native of Fenghuang, Hunan, has a master's degree in education from Columbia University in the United States. Since returning to China in 1927, she has served as the director of the First School of the Xiangshan Orphanage in Peiping on a completely voluntary basis. For the past eight years, she has worked hard and diligently, and the Xiangshan Orphanage has become well-known both domestically and internationally. She is now taking on the mission of overseas inspection at the invitation of the China Child Welfare Association. She has completed all the procedures for leaving the country and is scheduled to depart at 2:00 PM today on the Kantiru Yun ship at the North Bund of the China Merchants Bureau, and will visit major child welfare institutions in England, America, Germany, France, Italy, Russia, Denmark, and other countries to inspect their latest scientific facilities, study their internal governance, and adopt their strengths as a reference for our country's large-scale child welfare undertakings. Xu Jianping, general director of the China Child Welfare Association, has sent several signed Western-language letters of introduction from Nanjing for Miss Xiong to use separately abroad. Several Western-language promotional brochures of the China Child Welfare Association have also been reviewed and handed over so that Miss Xiong can distribute them abroad, so that people from other countries can understand the latest progress of our country. It is reported that Miss Xiong will return to China next spring and plans to write a brief report on her overseas inspection for the China Child Welfare Association for reference. Those who will be at the China Merchants Wharf today to send her off include Xiong Xiling and his wife, Zhu Tingqi and his wife, and other relatives and friends of Miss Xiong. Chen Zhengfan, Zhang Yueru, Ding Bingnan, and other staff members of the China Child Welfare Association specially presented a flower basket to bid farewell and wished Miss Xiong a pleasant and successful trip.

Autumn Rains Reduce Agricultural Harvests

Since the beginning of autumn, the weather has been hot and humid, and the continuous cloudy and rainy days, although sometimes sunny, have caused the rice crops planted in the fields in the four villages to suffer from too much rain. Currently, they are in the process of bearing fruit, and the cotton planted in the low-lying fields has been damaged, with the leaves turning yellow and the cotton bells falling off. This year's cotton harvest is expected to be reduced. However, the rice crops are still largely unaffected. However, at around 10:00 AM yesterday, there was a light rain for an hour, followed by a large clearing and the red sun in the sky. After 2:00 PM, dark clouds gathered again and there was a heavy rainstorm with thunder. It finally cleared up at around 3:00 PM. According to the old farmers, this year's cotton harvest has been greatly reduced due to the heavy rainfall, which has caused the plants to wither and fall off.

Study of Public Bus Crushing a Boy to Death

Cai Chang, the seven-year-old son of Cantonese woman Li Ding, who resides at No. 284 Fair Road, was attempting to cross the road from north to south near Fair Road on East Seward Road at around 3:00 PM on the afternoon before yesterday, when Public Bus No. 15022, driven by Li Jinchizhi, sped from the west. The driver was unable to brake in time, and the right front wheel knocked the boy down and crushed him severely. The police immediately recorded the number of the bus and summoned an ambulance to rush the boy to Tongren Hospital, but the treatment was ineffective and he soon died. Li Zhaogen and other detectives from the Huishan Police Station were dispatched to investigate and transported the body to the Forensic Examination Office on Fellen Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court was reported to have sent prosecutor Guo Wei and others to the office to examine the body. First, Hua Detective Shen Baoshan reported the previous situation, and then witness Ge Xuda (transliteration), a Russian residing at No. 468 Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, testified that he was sitting in the bus on that day. The car had just left Fair Road Station when he suddenly heard a loud braking sound. He looked out the window and saw that the deceased had been knocked down, head south and feet north. He did not see how he was hit. Li Jinchizhi, 21 years old, from Shandong, who has been driving for three and a half years, testified that when he had just started the bus from Fair Road Station, he saw a dilapidated car in front of him, traveling in the same direction. He wanted to let the car pass, so he turned south. Unexpectedly, the child suddenly ran out from in front of the dilapidated car, causing him to be unable to brake in time and knocking him down. After hearing the testimony, Mr. Guo declared that the deceased boy, Li Caichang, had been crushed to death by Public Bus No. 15022 before his death. The body was handed over to his mother, Li Ding, who received it and returned to prepare for the funeral. Mr. Guo then instructed the police that public bus accidents were frequent and that they must pay attention to prevention at all times. He also ordered the driver to be careful in the future and not to cause accidents.

Zhang Diaomei Sues Li Chuanhong, the "Old Madam," for Restricting Freedom; Seizing Adopted Son and Not Allowing Him to Return Home

Zhang Diaomei, a native of the city and the Chinese manager of the Yufeng Foreign Firm on Jiangxi Road, now 53 years old, recently hired lawyer Ling Baihong to file a criminal complaint with the First Special Court against Li Chuanhong, the "Old Madam" (i.e., the former concubine of Navy Commander Lin Baozhi, also known as a former prostitute, surnamed Geng), for restricting freedom. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Zehan opened the Eighth Criminal Court for interrogation. The defendant, Li Chuanhong, the "Old Madam," did not arrive. The plaintiff, Zhang Diaomei, filed a case and testified that he lives at No. 54 Guling Road. I have three brothers. My eldest brother, Xixiang, has two sons. My second brother, Yuruo, is deceased and has two sons, Yiliang and Yixian. I am the third brother. Because I have no son, I adopted Yuruo's second son, Yixian (19 years old this year), as my heir. He was given to me to raise when he was one month old, but Yixian is also Yuruo's legitimate son. Because my deceased brother had many concubines during his lifetime, the defendant, Li Chuanhong, was a prostitute in a brothel and was taken as the second concubine by my deceased brother. At the same time, there were three girls, Dayuan, Eryuan, and Sanyuan. My deceased brother Yuruo also took Dayuan as a concubine, who then gave birth to Yixian, named Baozhi, with the nickname Jisheng. Later, Yuruo died in the autumn of 1918, and the defendant remarried to former Navy Commander Lin Bao, who was old and had no children. The defendant then had bad intentions. Initially, she always took Yixian to the Lin residence to play, claiming to miss him, and he would spend the night and return. They visited each other frequently. Last year, I moved to Pudong, and in May of last year, after moving back to Shanghai, they stopped coming. Although I have repeatedly gone to negotiate, the defendant has been avoiding me, actually seizing my adopted son, Yixian. Therefore, I have come to file a complaint. It has been confirmed that the defendant lives at No. 74 Tongfu Road, living with her son-in-law, lawyer Zhu Yuan, in the same place. Now, she is deliberately refusing to appear. Impersonating the Ningbo Tongshan Benevolent Society, Scamming Donations Exposed, Li Guangyu Ultimately Undecieved

Gu Changsheng, a thirty-year-old man from Ningbo, along with two fellow villagers, Wang Agen and Zhou (both at large), held a fake donation book forged in the name of the Ningbo Tongshan Benevolent Society. On the afternoon of the previous day, they went to the home of Li Guangyu, a fellow villager and fishmonger residing at No. 49 Caishi Street in the French Concession, and coerced Li into making a donation. Initially, Li refused, but Gu and the others took out the "Credit Record of the Siming Public Association" published in the 23rd year of the Republic and showed it to Li, saying, "You donated five yuan before, how can you refuse now? You should pay the same amount," and so on. Li was taken aback for a moment and, finding himself at a loss for words, agreed to donate five yuan. However, after writing in the donation book, Li remained suspicious. He pretended to ask Gu and the others to wait while he retrieved the money and secretly called the Siming Public Association to inquire about the matter. He then learned that Gu and the others were fraudulently soliciting donations. He stalled for time, and the Siming Public Association reported it to the French Concession Police. When detectives arrived at Li's home, Wang Agen and Zhou, being alert, saw that their scheme had been exposed and seized the opportunity to escape. The detectives only managed to arrest Gu and brought him and the donation book to the police station. Yesterday, Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the Criminal Division No. 8 of the Second Special District Court's Police Affairs Department, stated that the defendant was arrested for fraud and forgery. As the police still needed to investigate and apprehend the accomplices at large, he requested a postponement. Subsequently, the plaintiff, Li Guangyu, recounted the defendant's extortion. When questioned, Gu confessed that Wang Agen, who was at large, hired him to solicit donations and he did not know the truth. Ding Wenyuan and Jin, accountants dispatched by the Siming Public Association, also testified that the Ningbo Tongshan Benevolent Society was originally located in Ningbo and had been dissolved in the 23rd year of the Republic. After Judge Chen Pusheng verified the testimony, he announced a postponement until the 13th for further questioning, and the defendant was remanded in custody.

Li Wanchun Arrives in Shanghai to Perform

Li Wanchun, a famous actor who has recently been extremely popular in the capital, is the son of the famous painted-face actor Li Yongli. His mastery of martial arts has reached the pinnacle of perfection, and his movements and postures all possess measure. Compared to the actors of the Shanghai school, there is a world of difference. His God-given voice is clear and bright, with a jade-like smoothness and roundness. Among the talents of today's theatrical world, he can be considered second to none. Furthermore, he possesses an elegant temperament and, apart from acting, enjoys painting flowers and plants, inheriting the legacy of Li Futang. He also occasionally writes regular script calligraphy with fluent skill, displaying well-honed artistry. Mr. Chu Minyi, a member of the Central Committee, even personally wrote the four characters "Da Ya Bu Qun" (The Greatly Elegant Are Not Commonplace) to present to him, which can be said to be appropriate and fitting. The Rongji Gongwu Stage on Edward Avenue in this city, admiring his great reputation, spared no expense in hiring him to come to Shanghai. Although Actor Li once performed in Shanghai as a child, earning great praise, it has been eight years since then. Having been away for so long, he greatly desires to take this opportunity to meet people from all walks of life on the red carpet and happily accepted the invitation. Yesterday (the 6th), he arrived in Shanghai from the capital at 2:00 PM on the 9:30 AM express train, accompanied by Mr. Zhou Jianxing, the stage manager of his theater. The staff of the Gongwu Stage and various box offices welcomed him. Amidst fluttering flags and the music of military bands, Actor Li and the members of the Yongli Theater Company emerged and shook hands with the welcomers one by one. Actor Li was wearing a white wool suit that day, displaying his heroic and extraordinary bearing. He then boarded his own car and sped to his residence. After resting for a few days, he will take the stage. His signature plays include "Lin Chong's Night Flight," "Qunyinghui" (Gathering of Heroes), and "Wu Song," all of which are masterpieces he is skilled at performing. The people of Shanghai will have a feast for the eyes.

Kang Le Special Issue

Valuing Reputation More Than Fearing the Law

A materialistic society most enjoys spreading the bad names of people. For example, if someone occasionally smokes opium, those who know will broadcast it to the public. So-and-so smokes! He is already addicted! He has fallen from grace! Or, if someone is truly addicted, but only smokes three to five fen per day, the spreaders will exaggerate and say: So-and-so has to smoke dozens of yuan worth every day! His family fortune is exhausted! Even worse, there is someone who smokes because of illness, but only smokes a little in the morning and is very restrained. He is able to arrive at the office on time and does not delay any public affairs. However, the spreaders will say that he is extremely lazy and has abandoned everything. If someone wants to hire him for an important position, the masses will destroy and stop him, saying: So-and-so is lying in bed all day and has become a useless person. He is not capable of holding a position! If he, for this reason, resolves to quit, and never smokes again, then the neighbors and relatives will quietly say nothing. No one will be willing to spread the news that he has quit smoking. Alas! The morals and minds of the world are so shallow! They only like to publicize the faults of others and bury the good deeds of others. It is as if this is what is divided and appropriate. Those who suffer the injustice and pain of being slandered for smoking are countless. If someone is not extremely foolish and wicked, who would not cherish his reputation? Therefore, in persuading people to quit opium, it is appropriate to advise and punish each person's reputation and concept. Those who can quit, public opinion will reward them. And help wash away the past slander. Give them a way out in life. Those who are not absolutely forced to quit, the social masses abandon them. Disqualified from the upper class. Never have a job. Then people are all frightened by the bad name of smoking, and they are still lucky to regain their reputation after quitting. Is not necessarily through judicial punishment, fines, and will be able to inspire smokers to quit. Otherwise, some do not even know fear. If smokers are suppressed and humiliated too much, they do not know how to cultivate their sense of shame and cut off their hope of restoring their reputation. Then it must be more effective to persuade them with their name, instead of forcing them with punishments.

— Tang Jiazhen

Observing the above diagram, it can be seen that the various cells of ordinary human bodies are all very peaceful and without any disease of excess or deficiency (Figure 1). After smoking opium, all cells are stimulated and increased. At this time, the mind and nerves are completely moved and reach a state of excitement (Figure 2). — Wang Yansong

Relieve the pain of being blacklisted and increase health and happiness - Dedicated to the Kang Le Special Issue

Research on the Origins and Development of Opium (Continued)

— Jiannong

The era when opium was imported into China most vigorously was the seventh year of the Yongzheng reign of the Qing dynasty. At that time, the British shipped earth from Macau, importing about three thousand boxes per month. Each box contained forty tubes of earth. Each tube weighed a little over three catties. Each box weighed over one hundred and twenty catties. The boxes were made of foreign wooden boards and sealed with raw cattle hide. There were many kinds of earth. The best was called "Gongban". There was another kind called "Xiao Gongban", whose quality was even better than "Gongban". As a result, this kind of earth became a necessity for social interactions among the upper class. In addition, there were also "white earth" and "gold flower earth", which were similar to the current used earth pulp. At the time, they were not very popular. As opium was imported in such a steady stream and became a harmful habit, the toxicity gradually became apparent over time. As a result, there were measures to prohibit trafficking and smoking. The first ban on smoking opium was announced by the Qing government. It said that traffickers would be punished with the cangue and caning. Repeat offenders would be exiled to remote areas. However, those who smoked were treated as if they were sick and not treated as criminals. Therefore, there were many jokes at the time. General private traffickers often argued that what they were trafficking was medicinal material, not opium smoke, and were thus acquitted. The number of those who were acquitted was very large. The most ridiculous thing was that in the seventh year of the Yongzheng reign, Liu Shiming, the governor of Fujian, reported that Li Guozhi, the prefect of Zhangzhou, had obtained thirty-four catties of opium privately trafficked by the trade merchant Chen Yuan. It was proposed that he be punished with a military crime. When I proposed to personally question him, Chen Yuan confessed that opium was originally a medicinal material and was not the same thing as harmful opium smoke. I summoned the medicine merchants to identify and verify it. They all said that it was a medicinal material, a necessary product for treating dysentery, and could not harm people. Only when it was added to tobacco and cooked together did it become opium smoke. Li Zhiguo wrongly regarded opium as opium smoke, which was very absurd. He should be referred to the emperor in accordance with the precedents of the knowingly falsely accusing people.

The private trafficker's claim that "opium" was originally a medicinal material and not the same thing as harmful opium smoke was already ridiculous. However, Liu Shiming, the governor of Fujian, a high-ranking official, was actually deceived by a private trafficker's sophistry and publicly presented the contradictory language to the court. And the emperor, who was known as wise and enlightened, was also at a loss to understand the situation. It can be seen that although the import of opium was large at the time, only a small number of people smoked it. Its toxicity was far less than it is now. Therefore, there were still people who did not know what opium was, which led to the ridiculous statement that "opium and opium smoke are not the same thing".

Opium was repeatedly banned during the Qing dynasty. However, general treacherous merchants disobeyed and secretly trafficked as before. As a result, during the Qianlong reign, there was a second ban on opium. The ban was roughly as follows:

Domestic merchants who trafficked would be punished with the cangue for one month and one hundred strokes of the bamboo. They would be exiled to the border and serve as soldiers for three years. Officials and guards who committed the crime would be dismissed from office. They would be punished with the cangue for two months and one hundred strokes of the bamboo. They would be exiled two thousand miles away and enslaved.

Although this order once had some effect, it did not last long. The toxicity became even worse than before. As a result, at the beginning of the Jiaqing reign, the rulers made a great determination and resolutely banned it. They also abolished the opium tax. At that time, there were still cases of private trafficking and smuggling. Therefore, when foreign ships arrived in Guangdong, the trade merchants first had to issue a "certificate stating that the goods shipped to Huangpu did not contain opium" before they were allowed to open the hatches and inspect the goods. Those trade merchants who concealed and were found out would be punished more severely. However, the stricter the ban, the more secret trafficking there was. The toxicity also became more widespread. British merchants set up ships to store opium. There was an "opium dream".

They were anchored in the Lingding Island and Da Yu Shan areas of Guangzhou Bay. The ships that secretly trafficked opium even had armed fast crabs (the name of the ships carrying earth at the time). The shops that sold the opium were in Dayao Kou in Guangzhou. They also colluded everywhere with government clerks, runners, and patrolling sentries. Therefore, many officials and guards in coastal areas had private contracts that required them to pay a bribe for each box of opium that was imported. It can be said that they were the ancestors of the large companies and officials who protected the unloading of opium earth in Shanghai.

Miscellaneous Notes from the Yumeiren Hall (Continued)

— Dun Gen

Yanzi Ke (Swallow's Nest)

During the mid-Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, when opium was prevalent, opium dens were everywhere in Shanghai. These were commonly called 'smoke rooms'. They were generally large in scale and lavishly decorated, with secluded rooms and comprehensive facilities. Those who entered could sit, lie down, chat, laugh, call prostitutes, and drink wine—anything was possible. Furthermore, merchants competed to surround the guests and seek sales of jewelry, silks, paintings, calligraphy, and antiques. Guests would lie back and admire them with delight, unaware of the time of day outside. But after the Republic, as the opium ban became stricter, impoverished people risked breaking the law to sell lamp fuel privately. These were often located in cramped, dilapidated dwellings with makeshift beds. Opium smokers would huddle inside, appearing as pitiful as beggars. These places were then commonly called 'Yanzi Ke' (Swallow's Nest). At first, I did not know where the name 'Yanzi Ke' came from. Later, while visiting a friend's house in Guangdong, I heard my friend laughing upstairs. I went upstairs to look for him but could not find him. I looked up and glimpsed a small loft hidden behind the roof beam. I climbed up a precarious ladder and found that the loft was so low that one could not stand upright in it, so I slithered inside. My friend was sitting on the floor, wildly smoking opium with someone else. His foot was tapping on the roof tile. I could not help but exclaim in surprise. I suddenly understood that this was truly worthy of being called a 'Yanzi Ke'! The beams of a swallow's nest roof are similar to the secret rooms where people smoked opium, and the loft's low height is also equivalent to a swallow's nest. The reason for this arrangement is to allow the smoke to rise and escape through the roof, so that people downstairs cannot smell it. My friend said that most of the smoke rooms in Guangdong were like this. So, it seems that the 'Yanzi Ke' in Shanghai only adopted the name without the actual arrangement. Hehe.

Xiaonü Mohe (Filial Daughter Grinding Box)

Someone often smoked opium using an ox-tendon box, smoking it once a day, emptying the entire box each time. His residence was divided into three courtyards. The smoking room was located in the middle courtyard, while the bedroom where the opium was stored was in the rear courtyard. He always had his young daughter perform the task of running errands and fetching more opium. When the girl carried the empty box to the rear courtyard to get more opium, she had to pass by a large well. She would always carelessly wave her hand and make the box rub against the stone steps, making a loud sound as she found it amusing. The mouth of the box became worn out from the rubbing, so the body of the box gradually shrank, and the amount of opium it could hold decreased. However, the person did not know this. This went on for more than a year. The box was now just a bottom, and eventually there was no more opium to be held. His addiction had also been gradually reduced as a result. The girl's contribution was great. This is the incremental method in the various methods of quitting opium. The principle is the same as reducing the amount of addictive substances in medication, known as "diluting each cup." If one can persist in this method and implement it gradually, success is guaranteed.

Junzhong Yanbu (Opium Rags in the Military)

In the past, there were many smokers in the military, and judicial power could not reach them. I heard that the reason for Qi's defeat in the Jiangzhe War was the lack of "white flour" (白麵) in the military. ("White flour" is a hidden name for morphine. The military regarded it as more important than rice. Once it was suddenly cut off, the entire army was as good as dead and could not move.) Furthermore, the well-known brave generals Zang Zhiping and Yang Huazhao had soldiers in their divisions who would hang a short bamboo gun and an opium lamp around their waists, so they could stop at any time on mountain ridges or wild tombs, lie down, and smoke opium. Still fearing that the battle time would be too long and they would not have time to lie down and smoke, they would issue opium rags in advance before setting out. Each person would get one to hang on their chest, like the kind of rag that barbers used to sharpen razors. It was soaked in a large pot of opium paste, allowing it to absorb and saturate, and then it was dried by the wind. They could suck on it during battle for a few minutes, which would relieve their cravings. Their spirits would immediately be lifted, and there would be no interruption in their work. Their shooting accuracy would certainly improve.
